## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations (dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration and the features are position x, velocity v, and time t, matching second-order oscillator models written as x' = v and v' = dv_dt = F(x,v,t). Nonlinear harmonic oscillators typically combine a restoring force in x (often nonlinear), damping in v (linear or nonlinear), and possibly explicit time-dependent forcing/parametric excitation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = -c0 * x (linear restoring force, conservative oscillator)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-spring-damper in normalized form)
- Time-varying stiffness (parametric linear): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (parametric excitation, e.g., Mathieu-type)
- Duffing (cubic stiffness, hardening/softening): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (nonlinear spring with viscous damping)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (strongly nonlinear restoring force)
- Pendulum small-to-large angle model: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (sinusoidal restoring torque plus damping)
- Polynomial Liénard form: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**4) * v - (c3 * x + c4 * x**3) (general nonlinear damping + nonlinear restoring)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillation/limit cycle via nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator (nonlinear damping in v): dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillation via velocity-dependent damping)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-type drag with linear restoring force)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v**3 (strong nonlinear dissipation at high speeds)
- Dry (Coulomb) friction approximation: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * tanh(c2 * v) (smoothed sign(v) friction term)
- Externally forced oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (additive periodic driving)
- Duffing with forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (canonical driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Potential-gradient form: dv_dt = -c0 * v - (c1 * x + c2 * x**3 + c3 * x**5) (interpretable as dv_dt = -c0*v - dV/dx with polynomial potential V(x))

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force → dv_dt depends primarily on x (often odd in x for symmetric potentials), with no explicit v term.
- Linear damping → an additive term -c * v; produces exponential decay of oscillation energy in lightly nonlinear regimes.
- Nonlinear stiffness (hardening/softening) → odd-power terms in x (e.g., -c*x**3, -c*x**5) change frequency with amplitude.
- Self-excited limit cycles → damping coefficient changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (1 - c*x**2)*v or (1 - c*v**2)*v.
- Large-angle pendulum behavior → sin(c*x) restoring term; deviates from linear -x and yields amplitude-dependent period.
- Aerodynamic-like dissipation → v*Abs(v) term; energy loss grows ~v^3 and dominates at higher speeds.
- Dry friction/stiction effects → non-smooth sign(v)-like term (often approximated by tanh(c*v)); creates stick-slip and non-sinusoidal motion.
- External periodic driving → explicit cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) terms; enables resonance, entrainment, and chaos in nonlinear cases.
- Parametric excitation → time-modulated stiffness multiplying x, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x; leads to instability tongues (Mathieu-type).
- General Liénard structure → dv_dt = -f(x)*v - g(x); useful for modeling amplitude-dependent damping and nonlinear restoring in a unified way.

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v
Candidate formulas: 52

GT is the fixed function
\[
0.156062620221068\,\sin(t)\;-\;0.372947617362308\,v\,e^{-|x|}.
\]
Key structural requirements:
- The \(t\)-only part must be exactly a single sinusoid of \(t\) (no \(x\) or \(v\) dependence), and can be represented as a cosine with phase shift.
- The \(v\)-dependent part must be exactly \(-0.3729\, v\,e^{-|x|}\). The dependence on \(x\) is through \(e^{-|x|}\), i.e., it is an even function of \(x\). Any term \(v e^{c x}\) cannot equal \(v e^{-|x|}\) for all real \(x\) because \(e^{c x}\) is not even unless it is constant (which would not match).

Now check candidates.

1. \(c0\cos(c1 t+c2)+c3 v e^{c4 x}+c5 v\sin(c6 t+c7)\).  
   Can set \(c5=0\) to remove extra \(v\sin\) term, and choose cosine phase to match \(0.156\sin t\). But \(v e^{c4 x}\) cannot equal \(v e^{-|x|}\) for all \(x\). No.

2. Adds \(c0 v\), \(c1 x\), plus trig and \(v e^{c9 x}\). Set linear terms to 0 and extra trig to 0, still left with \(v e^{c9 x}\) vs \(v e^{-|x|}\). No.

3. Has \(v\), \(\sin(\cdot)\), \(v/x^{1/4}\), \(v x^2\), \(v e^{c8 x}\). You can zero unwanted coefficients, but cannot turn \(e^{c8 x}\) into \(e^{-|x|}\). No.
